Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly amazed, because it seemed that the belly had no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I touched the wound and inserted my hands so far that the woman was in a better state;
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and the woman felt better soon after, and immediately spat out a little bubble of air from her body;
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	and I didn't record this chapter further because, when the masters find a strange thing, they know how to put it aside.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the marrow to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the pressor, where one presses the books; and at each turning as each head of the ligaments.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	In every way, let the horns be more subtle in the constrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	and let the mouth of the shaft be of a certain size, and the margin of the trees be thus, and of a length of one palm and a half;
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	and in the meantime the ligaments should be of the same thickness as this fist, which is closed at one end and the other, about half a palm's length or a bit more;
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	and this thickness of ligaments is placed in the mouth of the marrow to open when one turns the corns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, more subtle and lighter in its resemblance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of the clamps.
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and it should have ligaments, as you see, of a palm's length, and two fingers wide.
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	and when you want to open the marrow of the entire instrument, then make the woman sit on a seat, her feet pendant and legs uncovered,
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	then put the two adjustments adjusted together in the marrow, and hold the head of the instrument down between her thighs;
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	then open your hand to the entire instrument, so that you have made the tenons equally, according to the quantity that you want to open the mouth of the marrow, until the bile does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all mounted above, and are multiplied in their similarities; and when the miry ones have appeared to them, so much more hasty is the opening, and higher are the men because of their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despise the instrument that you have not prepared, for their necessities are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the secondine is retained in the childhood, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold his arm, and then make him stretch out his condition, and hold your hands at the mouth and nose;
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	and let it burst through the skin, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If the skin does not burst, take a pot, and make a poultice or cover, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the marrow, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia lignea, and centaurie;
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	all these herbs, or some of them, are cut or put in water over the fire; then put a cane or perforated tube in the mouth of the mare, and another end in the mouth of the patient.
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and the tin so that the vapors come from within the mare; then it makes them expectorate, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondary symptom appears quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this treatment, and does not go away, then instruct the patient to put their left hand in a poultice of sesame or in a musculature of alto, and then apply it to the affected area.
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and hold the second one; and when it has been found, take it and stretch it little by little straightly, so that the muscles do not snap at the extraction;
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but it must be moved gently to the right and to the left, and then pulled; if it comes out and disentangles itself.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the muscle is constricted there, we have described the treatment of sternum, and of fumigation with herbs;
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not all that we have said, beware that you do not foolishly pull on the traction;
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the vein, you apply it to the hip of the woman, then the cleansing of the four-humor treatment;
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	if you purge and apply it again, and comes forth foul matter; but at all costs, when it purges thus, a bad smell comes to the stomach and head, and harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	It is necessary then to make fumigations convenient for this: none of the ancients have experienced fumigation with fresh and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument by which one fumigates the woman at the retention of the flowers and of the secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is to make a similar thing to a candle, and place a subtle head in the nature, and large heads above the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigations be on the coals, and the tar until it is exhausted, and recommend another one.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, thus it is stopped up by subtle syrup.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	then it is necessary to apply the poultice so that it penetrates to his finger, and does not touch the surrounding area of swollen flesh, and clears the lesion so it does not touch it;
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a soft cloth soaked in wine and oil, then the treatment of anointing until he is healthy.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not rest, then put or insert a piece of lead, and leave it there for days, and be careful when the infants want to go to their chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes these sudden swellings come from wounds or abscesses; it is necessary to cover that sudden swelling: if it is treated, then as we have said about the piece of lead.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula at the bottom
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from beneath the bottom are nodulation, and larger than those that come from beneath the bottom of the body, or in the space of the two parties,
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	if there is a fistula or several; and when that nodulation is ancient, if it works, and encounters moisture, which makes the white or subtle boil,
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and these fistulas are often persistent; and they are known by the fact that there is indigestion or flatulence when the patient makes indigestion, and sometimes suddenly jumps towards it.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the rod; and they reach just to the joint of the thigh, and just to the top of the hip.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one recognizes the fistula penetrating to the foundation, and not piercing.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And it is that you apply your index finger to the foundation, and insert a subtle needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is tortuosity, you insert a subtle probe of lead, or a horsehair, as long as you feel the probe or hair at your finger.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and it does not come from outside through digestion or flatulence, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it does not penetrate further; then hurry to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is close to the bladder or near the urinary tract, if it affects the urine, and cannot be soothed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is close to the joint of the hip, then the tendon comes close to the place;
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	If there is no twisting and the invention of pain inward, it is that he has bowed in, and there is no medicine that can be applied suddenly by anointing;
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these persistent fistulas there is no cure except through labor, and the foolish doctors who intervene are useless.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In one that is not persistent and not ancient, there is hope of health through iron, as I have experienced.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and it is that the patient places himself between your hands on his back; and lift his legs up to his hips, and have his hips inclined towards his stomach;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then apply a tent of thread, or of lead if there is twisting, until you know where the tent goes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it at the bottom, then it is necessary that you apply your finger index.
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	then feel whether the thread has penetrated; and so discover where you feel between your finger the siphac or the flesh, then know that it is pierced.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if you do not work on it, one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One does not thoroughly heal all wounds, but it happens rarely;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help that one does, if it is that one heats the subtle cautery according to the size of the fistula, as it was said before;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and the entire hot iron is inserted into the fistula, until it reaches the bottom; and do this two or three times, as long as you know that these cauterized wounds are scorched, which resemble a bird's feather pen.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then treat the moist wounds with burdock, as long as those wounds are open, then treat the joints with ointment, softening and soothing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If he is thus healthy, it's good. If he is not otherwise, he cannot be healthy;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and hold it between, and do not pierce just to the finger that is at the foundation, and between your finger and the holding a thick covering of flesh or of skin, and you see the fistula at that which teaches the covering of the vein;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you cut at the beginning of the fistula, and apply beforehand to the holding, and then use the cautery, until it reaches the head of the holding;
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and the holding will be freed, and it will fall away; then I will show you those withered skin flakes that resemble a bird's feather, and none of them will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if you feel faint, and shorten between you and the vein, then cautery with fire or medicine is necessary.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the fire cautery assembles in this way: it is to know that it counteracts the effects of bad humors, and the drying of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then the treatment of swollen limbs in bath or with broken bread, as long as the juices flow freely, and it makes the bad humors flee from the bowels.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then heal the wound of the joints suddenly inflamed with dry charcoal, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	Because when it is restored, then it is healthy and does not relapse again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes almost to the font of the foundation, and is separated from the body, then cut off your finger or foundation, and inquire about that.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the tension, and between two is the membrane or the syphac or veins, or it is near to piercing, if there are no other ways than the way of faith and hope, through the administration of one of the three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	where you cauterize as we have said, or you cut almost to the bottom, or if you can put tenses and cure as before.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too much into depth, that you do not cope with the tenderness which holds the foundation, and come back to the sensations by way of the voluntary senses;
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then the treatment, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps it will be healthy, or you will remove that covering and the bandage then, since it is held by the foundation, either by tension or by another appointed instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then define that faulty flesh which is in the wound, as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then study how to restore the wound, and to stop the fistula in the part that is above the foundation: if it is lighter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And sometimes they are fistulas in this manner: and it is when you push the tent into the fistula, and it is where it touches the bottom of the foundation beneath the skin above.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	if you take a perforated tent according to this form at the head:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And you push the twisted thread into it, and push the tent onto all the threads in the fistula until it reaches the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If she is pressed on the edge of the foundation within, then extract the thread of that which is pierced, so that you touch your finger or foundation;
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and draw the head of the thread, and assemble the two heads together, and hold one to the other, and let it be a day or two;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and restrain it no more, until the thread cuts through the flesh that is between the two, and heals;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then cure the wound so that it is sewn and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not penetrate, then make it penetrate in all ways that you can, unless it is too deep inside.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not suit to make a copper plate for the dressing wound if it is deep inside, and then the cure, as we have said, until it is healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spine-like instrument that one makes for the fistula, if it is very pointed at one end and cutting.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and not on the other side, because one should not cut where one should not cut, as you see here.
des emorroydes	of bruises
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Bruises are of two kinds: either they are deep in the foundation, like a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they cut short the blood flow.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and there is one or several, and they are far from the foundation and at the end of the foundation; but those that are far away have little moisture,
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and they cut short either a little citrine water or a little blood, and they have the color of the body.

et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the uncle cannot hold them due to moisture, then take them with a drapil, or a cushion, or a piece of chamelot;

ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	where you cauterize as it is said or chapter of cautery, then you heal with other treatments until they are healthy;

cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	when the patient cannot urinate, and if the thread is pulled from the bottom, then it is a light treatment;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and it is that you take them with your finger or nails, and grasp them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healthy, and fear not the incision by iron;
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	Here is the translation:
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and it should be of a large size; and hold the thread firmly, then touch the thread, and remove the needle, and do so with all the others, and leave it alone to correct the excessive bleeding of blood.

et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let it be until it heals, and when they will be healed, if you treat with ointment and other treatments, until he is healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	to dry the wounds or dressing
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often it happens that there is a burning of fevers in the intestine, and by constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you make a point of a small lancet or a single claw which does not allow it to become moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then heal it as long as it is swollen, just as it is necessary.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot be healed, then recommence the rubbing more forcefully than before, so that it bleeds much and becomes scarred.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal them as long as they are healthy.
dou fremit	two fremits
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A formica is a small false appearance under the body, and it goes much deeper in.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes the cold reaches the frost, and one feels it as if dead from frostbite, and it comes into all the body, and more in the hands than any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a thread of a bird's feather, or a strong thread from a voltur, and place that thread on the patient's arm, so that the circles completely encircle the arm.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand all around the thread so that you grasp everything around the arm, and put it in the background, and strip the arm of its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make a frame of a cord or iron in this form, and be subtle underneath and draw above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce, because you must hold at the finger, and press; And if you see, then cauterize the arm, as it is before or in a chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the cluster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never make a cluster of silver or copper, or of tin alloy or mesh; and never make these small and large instruments, according to those for whom they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those therefore which one prepares in the treatment of children who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the cluster, small and large, is above large, or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and there is a separation where the intestines should be tied, as you see, and the chest should be perceived from within; and it has one of the sides perforated, and on the other side.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and let the intestines be where you put the medicine in a bladder of beast or parchment, and let it be perceived all around with small perforations,
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and have between each perforation a thread of space, then put in these perforations a strong twisted thread of cord or hemp, and assemble the intestines as if it were a bag;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then clusterize; and that's the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And the medicine should not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head with a gentle touch of oil or albumen of egg, or similar thing, then apply it lightly.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	Then sprinkle the ministers with his two hands together, so that it is all visible, then extract the ointment, and lift the patient's legs to the pallet.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And if the medicine wants to exit, let it come out as much as it can; and if he sleeps one night completely, it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you treat the illness of decay of the stomach, and the medicine hastens to exit, then recommend it as much as it is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the morbid matters are at the bottom, or an abscess, so be the cluster as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and it is the shape of the subtle cluster above where the skin should be held in constraint:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken about the treatment of wounds in the division; now we will tell you about the cures of hands and of medicine, according to the accomplishment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places or locations where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	Here is the translation:
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	where they are made according to the laws of the body, so that it falls on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, for the memory will come back to its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, if you take care it's not a matter of stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is great,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt the appearance of an abscess: if you make it thus healthier on the cephalic side, meanwhile as blood comes from the wound, and the healing is contrary to the naval part;
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and abstain the patient from repletion of wine and of coarse meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to recover, let his meat be diminished, and drink no wine, nor eat any flesh.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and apply to the wound, a poultice of warm oil rose water treatment, or in wine steeped.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, apply to the wound, so that it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder, which I will tell a little later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and he has been burned, if you put him on some ointments, so that he may be healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a sword's cut and similar, and the lips cannot be assembled by tending, if they are assembled by stitching, as I will say about wounds of the belly, from the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	If the wound is uncovered from the bone, and it festers, and only holds for a little, if you cover it; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard skin in place of leather.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as tested and roasted meat, and also like poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find a wounded skin, and it does not adhere to the bone, so scrape off the entire wound, and pour on water, then heal.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if it has formed an artery in the wound or vein, which without crust, and it cannot be staunched by medicines, so seek out the artery, and if you find it displaced, then tie it off with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if that does not benefit at all, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and it is that you apply this powder which absorbs in such a way that the wound closes up.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of the powder is this: take incense, one part; dragon's blood, two parts; living chalk, three parts, and subtle powder.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the poultice, and hold it firmly in place, until it adheres well and joins with all its sap.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it well, and leave it without loosening, so it does not become inflamed; for one does not stop the medicine until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at no time does one make a poultice of living chalk solely, when one has not incense nor dragon's blood, but rather the arsenic has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the artery has moved away from the wound, meanwhile in this state, if you do not put this powder;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but instead apply some digestive ointments, or poultices made of wheat flour mixed with water and honey, until it throws off the pus;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal other wounds as long as they are healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pinches;
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you about the breaks of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it's the nerves, there is no other remedy than to let them heal, and not to put anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and makes them retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the essence of nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but let the medicine be soothing, as you wash it in warm water, and mix it with rose oil, and cook it in warm water also,
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other wounds of mine according to this method, and apply moist unguents.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, sew it up with thread, then treat it until it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and it is hairy and full of pus, then pierce or lance below the level.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and as a result blood flows out, then stop it, and bind it, and cauterize, this is the task.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the veins, and the conduits are guarded, because that's where the nourishment goes,
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	if you cut the vein on the side of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then hold it firmly, and let it be for some days, then treat the wounds with ointments until they are healthy;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, seek the one that is;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are pieces of bone, seek those that you can remove, and those that you cannot have, let them be until the wound festers;
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and let it be disinfected and aligned with the outlet;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle on the powder that I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has become fistulous, then make the treatment thus as I said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	from a wound of a spear or dagger
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a blow of a spear or dagger, and the wound is very deep, then consider whether the wound is venomous, as soon as the patient becomes weary: know then that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep, and it is fresh in all its blood, then do not put the powder at the first hour, nor bind it with a bandage that does not press deeply into the wound.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and return to the body, and relieve the patient;
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put an attractive ointment on it, and bind it with a strip of cloth twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you have no ointment, put much cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture,
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on the wound for two or three days, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if he does not come to spasm, nor bad trembling of heart and there are no signs of alteration;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good dispositions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Heal then with tents and other treatments, until he be healthy;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if she cannot heal, and operate, then it is known that there is a fistula; if the treatment is as one must.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is simple, or in the front or back, then treat what is in front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, with stitches; and if it is small, with powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and has caught pieces, thus cure the wound, and remove foreign bodies if they are dislodged.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not dislodged, then let the wound putrefy, thus loosen the extractions.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and of other wounds the judgments of other members are so as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	because of the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great and mild and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the great wound sometimes the intestine, or the knots of the intestines, because of the intromission of the auspices;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the stitching is more troublesome, and sometimes it is worse than the small wound that the great one;
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because one puts back the intestines in, so one does not put them back from hot to hot;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell so much that they feel cold, if they return again to the points,
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and because it makes the putrid wound worse, because one puts back the intestines in their place that is theirs.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to three manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the common stitches have a stitch in the belly wound,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the stitches of other wounds on the body and these proper stitches are common to other wounds;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and however they are more suitable with the belly wound, and I will describe each one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestine is outside,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and this thing is to reset, it is by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	for the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestine is swollen from the cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is chilled, warm it up in such a manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	wrap an esponge or a cloth in warm water and apply it gently,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you cook in warm water and sprinkle and splash,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and raise the intestine until the inflammation is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and often make these remedies restraining, and it is necessary that they be soluted to remove the inflammation.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the inflammation depart, if you moisten the intestine with water or wine, and may it be cooked.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for by that is loosened the entry to a little thing;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a little wound at the instrument with which one gathers the blood clots;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is to reduce the swelling that is the size.
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we must not cut without great necessity there is;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and it's the instruments for the wound:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut within the curve and do not dig in, and see there the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine bursts forth,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if you reset it according to its natural form in its proper place
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	see thou in power, for this is worth many.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large, and it is on the lower part beneath the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	if it is necessary that you make the patient sit up on their back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and place his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the lower part beneath the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	if you place the head and the foot higher than the lower parts,
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the aforementioned parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	Here is the translation:
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to administer what I say for large wounds and injuries.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds, use what has been prepared for you,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then put it between your hands, I mean minister gently so that you hold the entire wound in your hand,
et assemble les levres;	and bring the lips together;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and it's the common manner of stitches,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and it is that you prick with a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave at the head of the wound, I mean a thread of space, and fix a needle or it has a strong twisted thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the joints of the skin with the joints of the underlying tissue,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is beneath the skin within, so that you make it penetrate to that part of the body
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and join the joints of the head where the veins are assembled;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then strain with a double thread within the needle of the vein,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then join the joints of the wound together gradually,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then let it cool down for a while, and he should stick another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then thread the wire as you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not cease from doing so according to how you have mastered the needles,
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until the whole wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and let the thin needles be between subtle and thick,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	for the thin needles take in all the flesh, and those that are too thick cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	because it is necessary that they be moderate;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it is not necessary to push the needles too far into the flesh and tender skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	that they do not touch and open the wound before the suture;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then touch the heads of the needles, so that they do not bother the patient while sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I hold tight or wrap a cloth around the heads of the needles to keep them steady,
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and let them be until the wound is sutured;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this manner of cauterizing with needles is more suitable for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	for it suffices to introduce a needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second cauterizing is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you assemble the two heads of leather and the two heads of silk together at a needle or where there is a strong twisted thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you will have perceived these wounds thus: three. together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	if you reset the needle at the part where you started, in the manner that one cuts the threads;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put space between each stitch the thickness of a smaller finger;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitch follows the bone,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I treat a wound one of my men had in his belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was wounded by a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm's width in size,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it was deep into the intestines, well nigh .ij. palms of size,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and it was the wound in the midst of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I returned the intestine then, for it had been that way 23 hours before.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was sewn up to the 15th day, and it was cured, and it was healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctor had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and do not cure with ointment, for I was standing in a place where one could not find any, nor any medicines;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I treated it with cotton very gently many times a day, and I washed it with honey water until he was healthy.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the proper ways of suturing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and sew up the part that is injured just up to the place where it is deeply wounded;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when she has pierced the right vein correctly, if you have placed the head of the syringe or costumed or thrust in the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make a hole in another part of the inner section up to the point of failure;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this stitching is that you sew thus as the pelletier makes the pellets,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and let the syringe flow from one part, and take it back from another, until the stitching is completely accomplished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second way of cauterizing, which Galen properly described,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	if it is like a spring, which naturally assembles the broken parts together,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one head to the other head, in such a way:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	fix a needle or a pointed instrument near the mirror, and make it pierce the joint just enough,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and let the heads of the joints swell up;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle and make it pierce through the weak part just to the inner depths,
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as the heads of the joints swell up;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then pierce one and the other through the weak part just to the inner depths, in the other joints that are swollen with mirrors that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and it's the worst manner of fracture and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galien says this in his book, and none of them testify to it,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one should cauterize the belly with .ij. needles, or have a thread in each one;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one should push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew up wounds;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and knows that when the rupture is within the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	if it is the seam more grievous than the other seams of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of the other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the fresh wound in all its blood, thus that the arrow has moved,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	Here is the translation:
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if it has moved, set a bandage on some joint that is affected, so the wound does not swell.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut the thread, and sew up the stitches, and the seam.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the wound as with the others, so that it be healthy.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you have no medicines, set on, as soon as it begins to gather pus, much cotton.
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and remove it often every day so that it may be healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you have no need of other medicine in many dispositions except when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound does not affect the principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	if it is necessary to soften the tendon lightly in oil of tempered heat, or in oil of rose;
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and put it between the fingers, and beneath the soles;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or pruritus in the belly, and many times it happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if they give a clusters of red wine tempered, and meanwhile the pruritus reaches just to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce deeply, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine that is called "fasting" cannot heal when it is wounded.
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it's because of the weakness of the veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of the entire body, and the approach to its natural constitution.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the scar heals from the wound, it resets similarly as the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it becomes old and turns to black or green, then it's necessary that you lift the black skin, which is removed from the blood that comes from it.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	because there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the ligament,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the joints in a position below the wound until it befits to align the extraction when the nerves are cut, and the wound is swollen.
de la routure dou boueil	from the rupture of the loose bone
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is relaxed, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	if it can be restored in some ways,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw that a man was wounded or pierced by a spear in the belly;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and was swollen and became fistulous, and thus he lost his digestion and windiness.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I put a treatment in accordance with what I was able to do, and did not cease from subtling until he was healthy, and the limbs were sound.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him sound, I doubted that the patient had a bad thing in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and he had no pain, but remained in better disposition, and eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and they direct certain experimenters that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied up in such a manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take firm hold of large sutures, then assemble the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the sutures have covered the mouth, then place them on the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it stretches its mouth open;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then he cuts the head, and this holds so that it cannot dislocate,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then set another fracture in the same way as before, until the wound is completely closed;
et cout la plaie.	and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	If the head sticks in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can bind the intestine with a subtle thread that is taken from the intestine of a beast,
en teil maniere:	in such a manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the head of this intestine thread that is very delicate,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then attach it to the head of this subtle twisted flaxen thread,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	Then put the thread in the needle, and sew up the intestine, and reset it in its route.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of stitching the intestines is not forced except according to the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, similarly when it is in one of the gut intestines, so there is no ingenious remedy, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it is swollen, is commonly called a "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and similarly when it is bearded and has a hollow bowl.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the truth a hard, dry, and white nodulation, where one does not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is also bearded like the feather of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes in clear ulceration, and sometimes dense;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	and sometimes little, and sometimes enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not clean, and there is no flesh;
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	this is not done except by one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	it is to know, by the small passage of blood or flow;
ou por sa malice;	or through its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh within, and on the lips, which does not let anything be born;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or where there is too much swelling;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	where the juices are rotten, and the material is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	where the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	where because the corruption is a kind of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	where the property in the region is slow in digestion, and slow in health, and feeble by nature;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	where there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the medical treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or it is necessary that I teach you to know the treatment of fistula which is done by hand operation.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that fistula occurs in all tender parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	because there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or at the spleen, or in the intestine, or in the bladder, or in some of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or at the spine of the back, or at any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it reaches the property of the principal member, and similar things.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are grievous wounds, and there is no remedy but labor, and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not heal quickly up to the place I have told, and you have confidence in the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you consider the view, if you take a probe of iron or steel, the fistula is straight, if it seeks;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, seek it with a subtle probe of lead,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	because the fullness is compressed within the twistedness;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and it forms a fistula in perforated hands and you cannot search for it well by palpation,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if you cleanse it through one of the perforations,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	because the moisture flows from one perforation to another, and it becomes putrid;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then you should examine your power to know if it has bone or nerve, and it is shaved in the foreground
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain they feel when pressing with your hand, and the place where they feel it
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is near a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I have told you, cut according to what I have told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and let the putrid flesh and rotten humors that are within;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the treatment so that it be healthy,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well perforated in the right place, it is necessary that you cut in deeply, as much as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I apply soothing remedies in medicine for fever, and the poultices just at the head of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	as long as the medicine corrodes the surplus which is accumulated at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put ointments on the wounds, so that they be healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healthy through this, then cauterize as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve does not bother you in your principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered, and there is decay and blackness, so let the king remove as much as the decay is entirely gone,
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal the things that are injured in the flesh as much as it may be healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healthy, and render void what was before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	You know that you are not a lazy doctor just until now:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if you uncover and seek as long as you are at the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healthy, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	Here is the translation:
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy than to let nature do its work;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if it has a small corrupted bone, and you can treat it with tourniquets,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if the instrument is suitable for that purpose,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if it has many bones, then remove them completely, do not leave even one;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if you make him contrary moisture, there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	if you bind and moisten and warm, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot dislodge them for an hour, then place on the wound a poultice made with rotten matter,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it be until the pus is rotten among the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then if they have lighter bones;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it's a large bone, such as a leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you extract so much of the corrupted material that the blackness is completely removed,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of the body corrupted, it reaches just below the shoulder bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it is necessary to open and uncover everything up to the corruption, and then treat it until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so take this example and help with your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of around 30 years, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within his body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	until the materials came to the leg, and it was inflamed with a large abscess, and there was no way to evacuate by opening;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the physician, in their foolishness, operated so much that the abscess opened,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and they corrupted many materials, and it became a fistula, and there were many perforations that all gathered together in a wound and moisture of the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many a mirror mirrored cure within these ten years, and there is no wisdom in the art of hands,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	until I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they cured him,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and those that corrupt through the openings of a large body;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young boy became red, and had a citrus color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I thrust a tent in one of these perforations, and then I sought out all the perforations.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hastened then, and cut into one of the perforations as far as I discovered a part of the bone.
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came just to the bone within;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I saw that which appeared to me from the corrupt bone, and I believed that there was no other corruption, except for that which I removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines, applying them gently over a long period, and could not suppurate;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I recommenced, and discovered the bone as it was beforehand,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found the continued corruption in the bone, and I saw it, and then I removed it, and I thought about suppurating the wound;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not do as much as I grasped around a palm of the bone, and it drew to all its mole.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored the administration of medicines; and he was quickly healed and suddenly.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it was no longer necessary to start the work again because of the weakness of the patient, who could not suffer.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and for the fear of death that I had concerning him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For the evacuation of blood often happens, but it was completely healthy.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and a hard crust formed on the bone, and it was of good disposition and had no harm or contradiction in anything, neither to go nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take the bandage and bind it to the head of the bone that is open,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command him to extend it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another strap of leather which is thicker than the first strap, and tie it on the flesh that is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the head, so that you draw out the corrupt flesh from below,
