et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh above the bone where you see the ulcer, so that the ulcer does not spread to the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and apply a firebrand or a hot tile below the bone to cauterize the corrupted flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to search how one can see and feel the corruption, and search again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	if it reveals the whole flesh; then apply a firebrand below,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then the decay spreads from one part to another, and is the putrefaction of the length of the decay; for it is a small thing, as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut off the corrupted joint, and decay spreads from one part to another.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuity of the joints, then there is no other remedy than to amputate.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the grasp of the hand or in the grasp of the foot, then it is very strong that thing.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but however it is necessary that you inquire about this decay, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and examine it in all the ways that you can, but so that the vein or nerve does not contradict you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the incisors and the teeth are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and the appearance of the mouth,
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and their subtlety, and their greatness and their smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason it is necessary to prepare each similar appearance of work with his instrument;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the instrument about which you have mastery, according to the knowledge of this art,
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and it will testify to the methods of the diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you prepare the instrument about which you have mastery, according to what is necessary for it.
dou feu	for fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	They burst out either because of an internal cause or because of a fever;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you will have medicated that corruption through the treatment with medicines, and it does not improve at all,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then you must amputate that limb up to the place where the corrosion comes from,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	if the patient is crippled by fear of death, or by wickedness, which is greater, from the defect of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the limbs turn black, as if they were burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and afterwards there is decay following the blackening, then there goes that corrosion of limb to limb,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and it takes over the whole body; if you hasten to copper,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is by the percussion of certain venomous beasts, such as a sea scorpion and viper and similar ones,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	the corrosion is at the head of the finger, thus the cope, and do not give it space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, thus the cope at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, thus the cope at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and it is not worth mentioning the few strengths of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and so then do when the corroding comes or falls: if it comes at the first joint, then the head afterwards at another joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and whether it comes or falls, then the whole foot is affected;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it rises to the leg, then it affects the joint of the knee;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to let the patient die of it;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the manner of coping with or saving the limb is that you bind it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and stretch out one minister below, and another minister above,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you detach the flesh that is between the two ligaments at a spacious interval, so that the bone may be uncovered;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	Then take the scoop or silk, and place a piece of linen there, so that the silk does not touch the healthy skin.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and bring to the patient another lesion and abscess wound.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if a flow of blood comes when you operate, then cauterize the skin hastily.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	where you apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is accomplished,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then lay the injured limb at a convenient angle, and care for it until it is healthy.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you that it had to do with a man whose foot was paralyzed:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a black spot that seemed to be burned by fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corrosion went first into his toe of the foot, so much that it consumed the entire foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man sees the decay, if he hastens to cover the foot, and was healthy;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long afterwards the decay returns or the pain of the hand, and it comes to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put him on things rebounding after the purification of the body, and could not stop the decays;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he saw that I bound his hand, and I did not want, that I had hope of rebounding the material;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I doubt also that if he cuts his hand, it does not die,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the strength of the man was weak; and he despaired entirely, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he stopped from cutting his hand, and was healthy;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not found it stated anywhere that because of this, one makes another treatment, so one has mastery.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	A boil sometimes comes to a head of charcoal, and stays for as long as it makes a large collection of pus.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it bursts and pierces, and the pus jumps out, and the dirty juices flow, just like a vase.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin that is above is as subtle as the thin sheets of a delicate cloth.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and it does not corrode only to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such a disease is called "healthy".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so prolonged that it reaches almost to the bone in the front, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is so thin that you can see the whole core, and similarly when it is subtle, just like a delicate cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it does not differ due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have seen that the skin is hardened, and the decay is not in the surface,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, if the treatment of clustering thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look if the ulcers are large, and the discharge that comes from them is of foul smell,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then the clustering of Egyptian medicine which is thus made:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Here is the translation:
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	as long as the medicine is red, and designates thus thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take of this according to your necessity, and make it into water and into honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and cleanse the wound with it, and hold back the pus;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine stay there for two hours, then extract it in sprinkling;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this many times, until the chest is exhausted, and the pus is removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and no time is it cleansed with water of ashes,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ashes from the wood of a vine, and throw water on top,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then boil, and cleanse, until you know that the chest is well purged;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot bear it, neither does Egyptian medicine nor the powder of ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	if they are to be treated with a mixture of water and honey or if there is a little bit of litharge ground into a powder;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	where you treat it with a mixture of honey and wine, so that the honey has the property of cleansing and washing,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the wound dry;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you are certain that the wound is well cleaned,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if you clear away what makes the flesh grow in it,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and it is that you take a definitive plaster, and make it with oil of rose and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you clear away some medicines and ointments, whose properties I have described in the treatment of ointments;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the small hole of the sinus is narrow, and the cane of the lancet cannot enter,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	if it widens by a finger's breadth, and inserts a tent of the Egyptian ointment,
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or ointment of basilicon, so that it may be widened;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too large, then cut and let it heal thus, so that the cane of the lancet can enter,
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if it pierces where the bow of the shoulder is above, whether it collects or further below the joint that it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bow is in the front, then do not let it bend downwards;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cope with the joint below, just as you have seen,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	if it appears in such a way that the bow runs to the lowest place that it is,
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	because when the bowel is perforated, they do not let it swell there
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the wound beneath just as you have seen,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	it appears in such a manner: that the bowel collapses gradually downward, and they leave nothing of the bowel;
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidating medicines to put on the wound,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and stand straight on the drapery of the linen that covers the whole breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then place the forces exactly at the nipple of the breast, a little larger than the first,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then adjust the bandage softly on the other drapery according to the quantity of the nipple,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and put it on the nipple of the breast to align the bandage, and do not remove the large drapery unless after many days, one time;
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and he who is above the perforated breast, often opens the bowel,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and knows that which runs from the bowel, whether it is venom or a little or enough, or digested, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and takes into account whether the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has been extended in such a manner and you see the nature that jumps above the perforated breast,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	Here is the translation:
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then dislocate it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you open the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	if it changes, I give another dressing, and renew the bandage.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the senses are upset by indigestion after many days, know that the senses are not yet clear.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if you take subtle remedies often after a long time, do not despair of your health.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	because the saints are near. Because there are men who take long to heal their wounds, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and it becomes indigestible that which is poured into the belly after many days, it knows that the breasts do not nourish anymore;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breasts take long to digest, and it is delayed, then apply medicines which are moist in substance and dry in virtue;
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	as we know definitively, because there is a great part of vitriol, and it is the last medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take a definite application, and they make it with rose oil, and the aroma of old wine equally in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then they concoct it and put it to use; and this same mixture makes honey cooked into a thick paste,
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when definite applications are not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	where you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind them, and powder them on the honey when it is on the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then apply glue, and spread it over the breast, and at no time does he administer an Aristolochy longer,
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of the celestial, which is as fine as flour of vezes and a hundred;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and in use of simples or of compounds: crush them, and make powder, and put on the honey that I have mentioned, and use;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the wound is elongated, and it is not cured by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that corruption is deep-seated, and makes an impression on the bone, or in the hard parts, or in the sinews;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if you treat a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the finger
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panarice is an abscess that grows beneath the fingernail, near the joint of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	where you tread, or by chance grow on other fingers;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is inflamed, and one does not take care, if an abscess occurs in the foot,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they run and pour forth a burst as far as it reaches the root of the nail, and by chance it reaches the whole;
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and there come ulcers up to the bone, so that a putrid pain comes, and it is the sign of a large wound, and the color is dark red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat them as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not profit them,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	you must cut away all the excess flesh that remains on the finger,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauteries are great aids if the bone is sound, and the finger is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and he approaches the flesh then, and begins to prick, and the blister.
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	it is necessary that you put the straight edge underneath the nail that does not touch the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and the end above, and cut the subtle and delicate flesh,
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and apply to the remaining flesh medications that are burning and corrosive to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the treatment of joints so they are healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then scrape it, and extract fiercely, for as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot be healed;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the decayed tooth, then scrape it in the name of us, just as it has been said before,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then the treatment so that it is healthy;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if he is wounded, and bruised, and he feels great pain, it is necessary that you heal him first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the corner of the spatula-shaped instrument, expertly cutting across,
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and beware that the cutting does not reach just to the flesh which is under the corner, for the patient would feel too great pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then put something on it that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain that comes from the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The two fingers that are born in the hands of some men by chance are entirely numb,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance there is a piece where it has bones, and sometimes it has a nail,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or their birth is in some of us of the two.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	He who grows in some new finger does not move himself,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and he who grows at the joint of the finger, perhaps moves;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the size of one who is withered is light, in such a manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	he measures it at its root by a large span.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Here is the translation:
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born or has a curvature of the spine, it is necessary that you first correct the round flesh up to the bone.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then correct the bone to a suitable joint for that, then heal until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The sudden swellings that come together at the joints arise from birth, or from a sudden wound, or from a burn by fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you correct the swelling, so that the joint returns to its natural shape.
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two warm tents or oil-soaked cloths, so they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you place between two subtle pieces of lead, so that the joints are joined, as it is suitable.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	They stick to one of these two with the palm, if you strike that joint as it is suitable.
Des vils	Of wounds
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	You see gross swollen veins full of superfluous melancholic humors that come into many parts of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they especially occur in the legs of those who go on foot and work and carry, rather than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary then that you administer sometimes a purging of the colon, and then the juice of the basil plant.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment of iron is in two ways: one is that they are struck, and then the black blood is drawn out.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and another way is that you open the vein, and pull out all the strength.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cutting should be done in this manner: raise the first leg to a warm and very hot temperature, so that the gross sinew is made subtle.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then stretch the leg of the patient downwards from the hip to the part below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut into the vein in one place, or in two, or in three, with a broad incision.
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then he lifts and draws the black blood to his hand, from one vein to the other, as much as it flows out like the virtue of the patient can suffer;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then he lies down, and instructs him to abstain from eating black bile-inducing foods;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and recommences the evacuation and the blood-letting when the veins are full, and annoys the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The elevations of it are according to this manner: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Then put him in a bath, and let the limb of warm water swell as much as it becomes red, and inflates the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bath, heat it with fire, and then apply it to the vein at the bottom of the thigh near the knee, or in the part below the joint;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the ankle, and scrape the vein of that part, as much as it appears when one feels it;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and you see it red and black, and when it enters the skin, it seems like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	Then apply the rule below, so long as it is lifted from the raw skin, and then attach it to the lighter ancone.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then shape in another way following the two joints; then scrape the skin on the vein as long as it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then leave it to settle, as you have done, and attach it to another uncinate bone, as you had previously done.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then shape another size, or more if you are a master of it, then leave it, and shape it to the toe of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then burn by fire cautery up to the second joint; then strip the fat from joint to joint, until it is entirely free, then the scab.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot burn by fire cautery and lift, if you prick with a strong double-threaded needle everywhere.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and lift and burn by fire cautery, and prick from beneath, and turn your hand on one side and the other, until it is entirely freed.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and beware that it does not form a scab, for if it forms a scab, you cannot burn by fire cautery or lift, and it causes harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have treated it all, put on the place of the wounded limb a millennial wine and rose oil ointment; and care for it until it is healthy.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the twisted and crooked and bandaged together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	so you must bend it gently, but do not cut it; and treat it as we have previously stated.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron instrument with which one cuts the twisted limb is curved, and does not cut too deeply, so that it does not cut into the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is of thick curvature, for if it was subtle, it would seize the vein, but be large as we have said, and this is the form:
De la voinne civile	Of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is located in the legs, in warm areas where there are no herbs nor trees, and in earth where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and perhaps grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this comes from the putrefaction that arises beneath the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	as it comes within the body snakes and worms, placing between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And the signs of the beginning of this vein are that it comes in the leg a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then it changes the veins, and begins to bud forth, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the head is open, it is necessary that you envelop with a piece of cloth one and a half inches up to the elbow, and the nail.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the splint stay on the leg, and every time it is not in default, if the swelling surrounds the splint, and the tumor;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut a part of it, and surround the remainder, and do not cut it in its root, until it is completely removed;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it returns to the flesh, and causes an abscess and putridity or pus, and a bad illness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because that is why it is necessary to treat it little by little up to the head, and leave nothing behind in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and it is not at all this vein when it is treated with 5 or 10 blows of a long handle, or of 10.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one hand comes to me, from which it issued 10 blows of a long handle, and when you touch it, if you feel a bone or a perforation, and pierce just up to the bottom,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	if it all issues out; and let the matter that is within be evacuated, and mix in the medicine injected through the pores without putting any more, then cure it as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And not at all this vein often moves, and likewise when it opens in the joint of the foot, or where the foot.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and many come from wounds, and where it jumps quickly; heal the wound thus as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	From abscesses that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "cow disease", because it often has cows,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it's a small abscess that grows between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the whole body, ascending and descending,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and he feels well along the length of the limb from limb to limb, as long as it straightens the skin or where it goes, and jumps forcefully;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is affected by an abundance of certain humors, if they come forth as worms and snakes and lice and ascarides or belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and doubt not of its evil, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	perhaps returning, and destroying the eye; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you want to cure and treat, if one cannot be strong except when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	it is necessary then that you lift the limb above and below with a strong, well-tightened bandage,
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut above and the tract force, and if the vein is deeply in the flesh, and you do not find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if you cautery with fire above, until it mortifies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does, if it runs to the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or near the eye, hold the eyebrow firmly, then cover above, and pull back;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is suitable to use the patient's purification of body by soluble medicines for the bad humidors pores,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and beware of rotten meats that cause putridity.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes into some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then moves from member to member; and I saw what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and I examined her arm, and saw a small inflammation in the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and immediately after, his veins appear as if a worm at the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more stiff than anything, as if living silver when it runs from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departs from that place, and settles in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little afterwards it runs throughout the whole body, until it reaches the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then I account for her that she turns again within the body, as if I see it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very amazed how she moved thus from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had seen that many had wanted to move the pain from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had not seen it, as I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and uncovered veins.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and because of this it appears that the constricted veins are wind-swept;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and I did not appear to be according to this reason among those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and restored veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you want to cure this disease, and the patients feel that pain, it appears thus as we have said.
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	Here is the translation:
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and burn the limb; and if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if you treat those who have wind in the stomach, as if making foul pills, and serpent's pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the limbs of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that they have large points, and small ones, and curly, and swollen.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those that have sharp angles, and those that have lengths, and those where there are fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and those that fall in no member if they fall in several ways: either in a principal member it breaks,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	like brain, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls then into no place of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you about later, appears.
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	it is necessary that you beware of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many cases;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this evil sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the signs of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and swells the soft tissue which is on the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	Here is the translation:
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it is without strength from the nostrils, or the ears; and perhaps it loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and jumps from the white moist wound appearing like a pouch, and it bursts out also like charcoal;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and this is a sign that appears, if you keep to the treatment, and extract the arrow if it is not inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the arrow when it falls or pierces, are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in a hard thing, not soft.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance the sieve moves also like the poultice, and in short black blood, and cold sweats come, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	it is then without doubt that death descends.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs of the arrow wound that never leaves a bruise on the skin are that without pus flowing from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs deeply and feels cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow wound reaches into the covering of the piss, it is beneath the small ribs; and throws great anguish and great pain and sighs; and moves all the members of the loins.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead or stomach, by chance jumps from the wound some undigested thing of the flesh.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead or belly, and it jumps into a point of feces through the intestine route, there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrowhead reaches the bladder, and the urine jumps and comes out forcibly, and the patient feels strong pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, such as the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the joint and the spine of the back and the forearm and the elbow and the legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to several more dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the vein is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, thus I will tell you what happened to me, because you should do otherwise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a certain man whose vein was cut or punctured at the root of the nail:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I touched it, and drew it out from under the fat of the ear, and it was healed without any harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I drew out a vein that was cut in the fat of the eye under the skin, under the papery layer.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was removed, and one cannot reach except for the tip towards the hollow.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and it was a large arrow from a Turkish bow, with a very light iron spear without ears; the game was healthy, and no bad accidents happened to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And it extracted an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I seized the barbs, and subtle as I was, I extracted it, and the Christian was healthy.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And he pulls out an arrow from the man, which was stuck in his belly, and thought that he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then when it had passed xxx days, it did not change its condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut around the arrow, and extracted it, and pulled it out strongly, and had no bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And I saw a man whose arrow fell out of his back, and the wound was sewn up above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and he keeps the arrow inside him, and does not change his natural disposition.
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	he finds no harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And you see another man, who had an arrow shot into his face, and the wound was swollen;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and he remained thus, suffering great pain; and many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And it happens to a vein at the man of the prince, the king, which was injured between his nails.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and it was a little declining towards the right side; and it was the entire vein that was reset.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to the treatment after it had been injured for three days. If I found the wound very constricted.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I felt it with a subtle touch, and did not hurt it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt aching and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the point of the arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on the wounded limb a plaster made with attractive and digestive ingredients, because the limbs do not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and it appeared to me that the limbs were affected by the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put the cautery fire in the usual place, and reopen the wound immediately, and delay thus the patient's long treatment.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he feels the arrowhead, that is, a day within his nose; and it told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put medicine on the wound, a corrosive medicine by usual means, until it was covered over.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and probed, and felt the head of the arrow which had stuck to the bone;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I apply to the opening of the wound by that medicated ointment, so that the head of the arrow appears visibly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and passes well the limits within three months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then I relax if the wound that I touched with the tongs, and my hand on one side and the other, and cannot issue.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I did not cease to subtily and ingeniously make devices, until I took it with well-made tongs on that day.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, as much as I trace it, and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the mirror shows that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I will restore it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was entirely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you about the quality of the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	if you put your treatment on those whom I do not mention, for the books cannot take everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters compare well a little great thing, and on those who are present and failing,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find a new work, and a new instrument, in the understanding of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that the arrows do not issue from the limbs where they are fixed except according to certain manners.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	where they enter through the skin, or through another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and the one that jumps forth where it enters, this is an arrow entering into their flesh, and it has jumped forth many times now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump forth now, let it be until the flesh is purified around it, and the exit is eased;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and thus if it is fixed in the bone, and it cannot exit, let it be so for several days, and the swelling will decrease each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it jumps, and if it does not jump, one pierces everywhere with a subtle finger, as long as the eyes in every direction are enlarged, and then the treatment.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is fixed in the bone of the head, and goes just to one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: if they do not treat it, but let it be until it is even after some days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow comes just to the eye, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is not fixed properly because it was not set in the bone, and does not come out by itself.
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient stays some days without bad accidents, if the engine of the draw does well.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very fixed in and cannot come out, then I will administer tareres around, as I have told you; then treat the limb until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is replaced in the body of the corpse so that one cannot see it, then it seeks to have all its tension.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel, if the sensation draws to no convenient instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound, and due to the depth of the arrow;
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone or vein, if the wound is so large that the wound is great;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and draw out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears on the arrow where it holds;
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if you remove the skin which is stuck with ulcers so that you can cleanse,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the wings of the arrow, so that you can extract it;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and subtly take care not to break the arrow, so that you extract it more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at one time, let it stay until the surrounding tissue is purified, then extract it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if you remove blood that does harm, then amend what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of the incision near the nerve and the vein, and set in motion a device so you can safely extract the arrow without danger;
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	whether it is hot or cold, whether firm or gentle; and place the patient according to the position he was in when the arrow fell on him;
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for it is the greatest aid that it can be, and if you cannot, then place it according to what the signs show you;
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another direction, where it appears as if nothing of it is there, or the skin is inflamed in this spot if one sees or feels it somehow:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut then thus, so that the tendons can take hold, and then extract: if it bursts out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, turn your hand roundly, so that it enters into the bone, and enlarges the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then recommence the extraction until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if it is the fault of the arrow, it is, he cuts all the fault;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if it is a chest wound, and you want to administer a treatment, if he administers. It is a cutting instrument;
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	if the point of the arrow enters into the head of the instrument; and then cuts forcefully,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is cut, he cuts the instrument to a point entering in, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the vein is touched, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the veins are, so you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then heal the wound as it covers.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the vein is in the hand or foot or belly or bladder or side, and it is nearby, and you can cut above, so you cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cut the vein and the nerve, and then extract, and then sew the wound, so that is the task.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the treatment as long as it is healthy.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to extract arrows are similar to a bird's beak, and see here the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways of doing so: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the instrument for extracting arrows is also similar to a bird's feather pen.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	To hollow out at the point of the arrow, thus it is the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the tongs to hollow out and to extract if it is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of the veins from which one bleeds are 21, where it has or the head 16.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	it is to know: it is a type of wounds that are behind the ears, which are called the two "herbech".
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the wounds arteries that are in the temples appearing;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the veins that are in the eyelids of the eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is on the forehead; and the vein that is at the head of the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the damaged sinews which are at the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the damaged veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the damaged veins that are beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic, and it is on the left side of the head, and people commonly call it "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the vein called "fast" is composed of the cephalic and the basilic;
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and people commonly call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein is on the right side,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and people commonly call it "vein of the belly", and it is located near the pubic area,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is the one which we bleed, which appears manifestly above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the saphena vein is the one that is between the auricular and anular, and if it has two roots;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and where the feet are, there are three veins: one is below the curvature of the left pouch side,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second saphena vein which is at the junction of the right side; and the vein called "nesse" which is at the junction of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and on the other leg are 3 veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The wisdom of the veins that are behind the ears helps with ancient cathartics and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the qualities of the vein, as I tell you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the place where the veins are of a rough cloth; then bind the patient's neck to a vice.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	as long as the veins appear behind the ears in the same way the dependencies of the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	where the hammers strike your finger, and where you feel the pulse beneath your finger, it is a sign of an inch;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet, and insert it beneath the vein just to the bone, then lift your hand above the entire vein above,
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and open the skin and the vein well, you should have two passages to traverse, and make the blood flow out as much as you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then hold it steady and lift it, until it is healthy;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The health of the two arteries that are in the two temples, if it is worth migrating to an ancient one,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and swollen, and accustomed to opthalmia, and at the course of the bitter tears that flow from the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the healthy person is thus as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient strains his neck, so much that the two veins appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse beneath your finger, and then make a sign of inching;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then raise the heart onto the vein above your finger's tip, and insert the lancet below;
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and elevate the vein high up, and the cupping, just as you have done with other veins, and correct the flow of blood according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then lower the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then place on cotton;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then form it firmly, and let it be until it is healthy; and we have already spoken of their cupping and their extraction, where the book begins.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The health of the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the health of the cephalic veins for ancient diseases of the face, and for migraines, and for redness;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is such that the patient strains his neck by twisting, so much that the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "fosseur", of which this is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and press with your hand, or with something else, and let the blood flow out according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then release the patient's neck, and hold the vein until it is healthy and never again affected by a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Here is the translation:
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The health of the 10 veins that are in 10 vessels helps the eyes, and the tongue, and the nose, and the little finger in the oil, and for diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their health is that the patients stretch their neck by twisting some ligament, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the health, and let the healthy part of the crossing, a little bit of the long, a little bit of the broad, for there is no point of flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps they break; then make a correction of the blood, as much as you have mastery, and then place it on the cushion, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The sanity of the vein where it doesn't get to the aque, and to strong foresight, and to facial diseases.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	as if it migrates and reddens when it comes into the face, and similarly when it is ancient;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the sanity is that the patient contracts his neck, then stretches his nose to his left hand.
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the subtle flame long, and fix it in the empty space which is between the two nostrils.
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein does not open well enough, and the blood will now begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not let it flow too much in depth, and make the blood flow according to necessity, then leave it a night, for it is nearly fully restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and that is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The knowledge of .ij. wounds helps with the treatment of anemia, and at the beginning of messleria, and many illnesses, and impetigo, and corroding, and herpes, and similar things;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the health is such that the patient stretches his neck now one way and then another, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master stand above the head of the patient, and the patient sits on a seat,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then let the vein of the loin be opened somewhat widely, then draw out the blood moderately, or as much as the master is able;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then make another incision in the other vein, then loosen the ligament, and hold the veins together moderately;
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	that the patient does not strangle; and let it just until morning, so that the wound be healthy.
De la sainie des leivres	About the health of the livers
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the veins above the liver is affected by gathering at the mouth, and corruption of gums, and cracks in the lips, and painful nostrils and within.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of health is to make the patient sit in front of you, and hold their neck steady as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	Then turn the lever, and examine the two veins, one of which is on the right vein and the other on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and they are recognized by this, that they are black, and by this, that around them there are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	touch one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	if you touch the largest of each part, and thus make the two veins that are above and below, because it is a similar manner.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	About the health of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The health of the veins that are beneath the tongue aids after the health of the head, and it's in the constriction of the throat, and in the diseases of the lips, and in the diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the veins is such that the patient's saliva falls between your hands before the sun, and lifts the tongue, and looks beneath each side for a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	examine one and the other, and do not go too deep in the font, because beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the skin which are commonly sained are sained in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	where we prick all over, it is a flame-like burning, or subtle olive-like if the cuts are deep, and is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame-like burning is very renowned, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veins with a scalpel showing large amounts of blood appearing, and that they contain much blood and turmoil;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and it's the form of the flame of olive oil:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtly pointed, and it is for clarifying the subtle veins, where there is subtle citrine blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The purification of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with the illnesses that are under the throat, and in the neck, and in the feet, and in the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the surgeon to make a gentle incision, and to beware of the artery that lies beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a flow of blood comes, it is necessary to staunch it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and one must not be touching the flame, but rather cutting as if with an anvil.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilic vein does not open clearly, it is necessary to extract it, and change to another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	where you want no vein of it, or you feel in its place the vein within the arm: it appears manifestly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the coping with the flame anesthetized, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to examine the place of the wound, it is necessary that you stretch out the arm, so that you touch the place as much as you feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place of the incision, and then stretch out the arm, and cope with the vein of the flame anesthetized;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware that you do not strike into the artery when you see the limb swollen, because it is of the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it swell up high like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is not from the artery:
